<p><b>Super Bowl XLV</b> was an <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">American football</a> game between the <a href="/wiki/American_Football_Conference" title="American Football Conference">American Football Conference</a> (AFC) champion <a href="/wiki/2010_Pittsburgh_Steelers_season" title="2010 Pittsburgh Steelers season">Pittsburgh Steelers</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_Conference" title="National Football Conference">National Football Conference</a> (NFC) champion <a href="/wiki/2010_Green_Bay_Packers_season" title="2010 Green Bay Packers season">Green Bay Packers</a> to decide the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a> (NFL) champion for the <a href="/wiki/2010_NFL_season" title="2010 NFL season">2010 season</a>. The Packers defeated the Steelers by the score of 31–25. The game was played on February 6, 2011, at <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Stadium" title="AT&amp;T Stadium">Cowboys Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Arlington,_Texas" title="Arlington, Texas">Arlington, Texas</a>, the first time the Super Bowl was played in the <a href="/wiki/Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_metroplex" title="Dallas–Fort Worth metroplex">Dallas–Fort Worth</a> area.</p>
<p>Unlike other matchups, this game featured two title-abundant franchises: coming into the game, the Packers held the most NFL championships with 12 (9 league championships prior to the Super Bowl era and 3 Super Bowl championships), while the Steelers held the most Super Bowl championships with 6. The Packers entered their fifth Super Bowl in team history, and became the first number 6-seeded team in the NFC to compete in the Super Bowl, after posting a 10–6 regular season record. The Steelers finished the regular season with a 12–4 record, and advanced to a league-tying 8th Super Bowl appearance.</p>
<p>Green Bay dominated most of the first half of Super Bowl XLV, jumping to a 21–3 lead before Pittsburgh cut it down to 21–10 just before halftime. Then after the teams exchanged touchdowns, the Steelers pulled within 28–25 midway through the fourth quarter with wide receiver <a href="/wiki/Mike_Wallace_(American_football)" title="Mike Wallace (American football)">Mike Wallace</a>'s 25-yard touchdown reception from quarterback <a href="/wiki/Ben_Roethlisberger" title="Ben Roethlisberger">Ben Roethlisberger</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Two-point_conversion" title="Two-point conversion">two-point conversion</a>. But the Packers answered with <a href="/wiki/Mason_Crosby" title="Mason Crosby">Mason Crosby</a>'s 23-yard field goal with 2:07 remaining, and then prevented the Steelers from scoring on their final drive of the game. Packers quarterback <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Rodgers" title="Aaron Rodgers">Aaron Rodgers</a> was named <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_MVP" title="Super Bowl MVP">Super Bowl MVP</a>, completing 24 of 39 passes for 304 yards and three touchdowns.</p>
<p>The broadcast of Super Bowl XLV on <a href="/wiki/Fox_NFL" title="Fox NFL">Fox</a> averaged about 111 million viewers, breaking the record for the <a href="/wiki/List_of_most_watched_television_broadcasts_in_the_United_States" title="List of most watched television broadcasts in the United States">most-watched program</a> in American television history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seidman1987_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-seidman1987-4">[4]</a></sup> The game's attendance was 103,219, just short of the Super Bowl record 103,985 set in <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XIV" title="Super Bowl XIV">Super Bowl XIV</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Rose_Bowl_(stadium)" title="Rose Bowl (stadium)">Rose Bowl</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pasadena,_California" title="Pasadena, California">Pasadena, California</a>. The halftime show featured the American <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a> group <a href="/wiki/The_Black_Eyed_Peas" title="The Black Eyed Peas">The Black Eyed Peas</a>, with additional performances by <a href="/wiki/Usher_(singer)" title="Usher (singer)">Usher</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slash_(musician)" title="Slash (musician)">Slash</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_Bowl_XLV&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Host_selection_process">Host selection process</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_Bowl_XLV&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Host selection process">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cowboys_stadium.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Cowboys_stadium.JPG/220px-Cowboys_stadium.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Cowboys_stadium.JPG/330px-Cowboys_stadium.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Cowboys_stadium.JPG/440px-Cowboys_stadium.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cowboys_stadium.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Stadium" title="AT&amp;T Stadium">Cowboys Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Arlington,_Texas" title="Arlington, Texas">Arlington, Texas</a> was ultimately chosen as the site for Super Bowl XLV.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Three NFL cities presented bids for the game:</p>
<ul>
<li>In January 2007, <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_VI" title="Super Bowl VI">Super Bowl VI</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_MVP" title="Super Bowl MVP">MVP</a> <a href="/wiki/Roger_Staubach" title="Roger Staubach">Roger Staubach</a> was named chairman of the North Texas Super Bowl Bid Committee,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dalbiz_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-dalbiz-6">[6]</a></sup> heading the <a href="/wiki/Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_metroplex" title="Dallas–Fort Worth metroplex">Metroplex</a>'s bid effort. The bid gathered the support of the cities of Arlington and Dallas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></li>
<li>On January 31, 2007, the city of <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis" title="Indianapolis">Indianapolis</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis_Colts" title="Indianapolis Colts">Colts</a> owner <a href="/wiki/Jim_Irsay" title="Jim Irsay">Jim Irsay</a> and Indianapolis Mayor <a href="/wiki/Bart_Peterson" title="Bart Peterson">Bart Peterson</a>, officially announced details about their intentions to bid for Super Bowl XLV.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> The site would have been <a href="/wiki/Lucas_Oil_Stadium" title="Lucas Oil Stadium">Lucas Oil Stadium</a>, which opened in 2008. They were eventually awarded <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLVI" title="Super Bowl XLVI">Super Bowl XLVI</a>.</li>
<li>On February 21, 2007, the <a href="/wiki/Glendale,_Arizona" title="Glendale, Arizona">Glendale</a> City Council came to a consensus to prepare a bid to host Super Bowl XLV. <a href="/wiki/University_of_Phoenix_Stadium" title="University of Phoenix Stadium">University of Phoenix Stadium</a> was already scheduled to host <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLII" title="Super Bowl XLII">Super Bowl XLII</a> in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-glendalestar_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-glendalestar-10">[10]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p><a href="/wiki/List_of_NFL_franchise_owners" title="List of NFL franchise owners">NFL owners</a> voted to select the <a href="/wiki/North_Texas" title="North Texas">North Texas</a> site on May 22, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Teams">Teams</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_Bowl_XLV&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Teams">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pittsburgh_Steelers">Pittsburgh Steelers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_Bowl_XLV&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Pittsburgh Steelers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2010_Pittsburgh_Steelers_season" title="2010 Pittsburgh Steelers season">2010 Pittsburgh Steelers season</a></div>
<p>The Pittsburgh Steelers finished the 2010 season with a 12-4 record. They earned the <a href="/wiki/AFC_North" title="AFC North">AFC North</a> division title, and the second seed in the <a href="/wiki/American_Football_Conference" title="American Football Conference">AFC</a> and advanced to their 8th Super Bowl, tying the <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Cowboys" title="Dallas Cowboys">Dallas Cowboys</a>' record of most Super Bowl appearances.</p>
<p>After missing the first four games of the year on suspension for violating the NFL's personal conduct policy (during which the Steelers went 3–1), quarterback <a href="/wiki/Ben_Roethlisberger" title="Ben Roethlisberger">Ben Roethlisberger</a> returned for his seventh season as the Steelers starting quarterback, finishing the season with 3,200 yards and 17 touchdowns, with just five interceptions, for a 97 passer rating. He also rushed for 176 yards and two touchdowns. The team's top receiver was <a href="/wiki/Mike_Wallace_(American_football)" title="Mike Wallace (American football)">Mike Wallace</a> who caught 60 passes for 1,257 yards and 10 touchdowns, giving him a 21 yards per catch average. Other reliable options included 13-year veteran <a href="/wiki/Hines_Ward" title="Hines Ward">Hines Ward</a> (59 receptions for 755 yards and 5 TDs), the Steelers all-time leading receiver, and tight end <a href="/wiki/Heath_Miller" title="Heath Miller">Heath Miller</a> who caught 42 passes for 512 yards. Halfback <a href="/wiki/Rashard_Mendenhall" title="Rashard Mendenhall">Rashard Mendenhall</a> was the team's leading rusher, gaining 1,273 yards and 13 touchdowns while also catching 23 passes. The line was led by rookie center <a href="/wiki/Maurkice_Pouncey" title="Maurkice Pouncey">Maurkice Pouncey</a>, the Steelers only pro bowl selection on offense. However, Pouncey was injured in the AFC championship game and would be inactive for Super Bowl XLV.</p>
<p>The Steelers had one of the league's top defenses, leading the NFL in sacks (48), and fewest points (14.5) and rushing yards (62.8) allowed per game, while ranking second in fewest total yards (276.8). The line was anchored by pro bowl end <a href="/wiki/Brett_Keisel" title="Brett Keisel">Brett Keisel</a>. The Steelers also had four excellent linebackers: <a href="/wiki/LaMarr_Woodley" title="LaMarr Woodley">LaMarr Woodley</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Harrison_(American_football)" title="James Harrison (American football)">James Harrison</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Farrior" title="James Farrior">James Farrior</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Timmons" title="Lawrence Timmons">Lawrence Timmons</a>. For the third consecutive year, Woodley and Harrison each recorded at least 10 sacks. Woodley also forced three fumbles and Harrison forced six. Farrior had 109 total tackles and six sacks. Timmons led the team with 135 total tackles, while also recording three sacks and two interceptions. The secondary was led by pro bowl safety <a href="/wiki/Troy_Polamalu" title="Troy Polamalu">Troy Polamalu</a>, who won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NFL_Defensive_Player_of_the_Year_Award" title="NFL Defensive Player of the Year Award">NFL Defensive Player of the Year Award</a>, tying his career-best seven interceptions and returning them for 101 yards and a touchdown.</p>
<p>Coach <a href="/wiki/Mike_Tomlin" title="Mike Tomlin">Mike Tomlin</a>, already the youngest coach to ever win a Super Bowl, became the youngest coach ever to make it to the Super Bowl twice at age 38. The Pittsburgh Steelers had also accomplished going to the Super Bowl in five different decades; and, in every decade since the post AFL-NFL merger. 1970s: 1975,1976, and 1979. 1980s: 1980. 1990s: 1996. 2000s: 2006 and 2009. 2010s : 2011.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Green_Bay_Packers">Green Bay Packers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_Bowl_XLV&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Green Bay Packers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2010_Green_Bay_Packers_season" title="2010 Green Bay Packers season">2010 Green Bay Packers season</a></div>
<p>The Green Bay Packers finished the season with a 10-6 record and became the first number 6-seeded team in the NFC to compete in the Super Bowl. They are only the second number 6 seeded team to reach the Super Bowl, with the only other number 6 seed to accomplish this feat being the <a href="/wiki/2005_Pittsburgh_Steelers_season" title="2005 Pittsburgh Steelers season">Pittsburgh Steelers</a>, who won <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XL" title="Super Bowl XL">Super Bowl XL</a> following the 2005 season. Green Bay also joined the 2005 Steelers as the only teams ever to defeat the top three seeded teams on the road in the playoffs. In order to secure their fifth Super Bowl bid they defeated their longtime rivals, the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Bears" title="Chicago Bears">Chicago Bears</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/NFC_Championship_Game" title="NFC Championship Game">NFC Championship Game</a> at <a href="/wiki/Soldier_Field" title="Soldier Field">Soldier Field</a>.</p>
<p>The offense was led by quarterback <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Rodgers" title="Aaron Rodgers">Aaron Rodgers</a>, who was in his third year as a starter after taking over for the team's all-time leading passer <a href="/wiki/Brett_Favre" title="Brett Favre">Brett Favre</a>. Rodgers finished the season completing 65.7% of his passes for 3,922 yards and 28 touchdowns, with only eleven interceptions, giving him his second consecutive season with a triple digit passer rating (101.2). He was also a good rusher, adding 356 yards and 4 touchdowns on the ground. His top target was pro bowl receiver <a href="/wiki/Greg_Jennings" title="Greg Jennings">Greg Jennings</a>, who caught 76 passes for 1,265 yards and 12 touchdowns, giving him a 16.6 yards per catch average while also ranking him fourth in the NFL in yards and second in touchdown catches. Other reliable targets included receivers <a href="/wiki/James_Jones_(wide_receiver)" title="James Jones (wide receiver)">James Jones</a> (50 receptions, 676 yards, 5 tds), <a href="/wiki/Donald_Driver" title="Donald Driver">Donald Driver</a> (51 receptions, 565 yards, 4 tds), and <a href="/wiki/Jordy_Nelson" title="Jordy Nelson">Jordy Nelson</a> (45 receptions, 582 yards, 496 kick return yards). The Packers lost star tight end <a href="/wiki/Jermichael_Finley" title="Jermichael Finley">Jermichael Finley</a> (21 receptions 301 yards, 1 td) to injury in week five who was their leading receiver at the time. The Packers ground game was crippled by injuries, especially the Week 1 loss of <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Grant" title="Ryan Grant">Ryan Grant</a>, who had rushed for over 1,200 yards in each of the last two seasons. In his absence, the team relied prominently on <a href="/wiki/Brandon_Jackson_(American_football)" title="Brandon Jackson (American football)">Brandon Jackson</a>, who rushed for 703 yards and caught 43 passes for 342, and fullback <a href="/wiki/John_Kuhn" title="John Kuhn">John Kuhn</a>, who added 281 yards on the ground. The team's offensive line was anchored by pro bowl tackle <a href="/wiki/Chad_Clifton" title="Chad Clifton">Chad Clifton</a>, an 11-year veteran.</p>
<p>The Packers defense ranked second in the league in fewest points allowed per game (15). The line was led by <a href="/wiki/Cullen_Jenkins" title="Cullen Jenkins">Cullen Jenkins</a>, who recorded seven sacks in just eleven games, and 338-pound defensive tackle <a href="/wiki/B._J._Raji" title="B. J. Raji">B. J. Raji</a>, who had 6.5. The linebackers were led by pro bowler <a href="/wiki/Clay_Matthews_III" title="Clay Matthews III">Clay Matthews</a> and <a href="/wiki/A._J._Hawk" title="A. J. Hawk">A. J. Hawk</a>. Matthews ranked fourth in the NFL with 13.5 sacks, while Hawk led the team in combined tackles (111) and intercepted three passes. Three of the Packers starters in the secondary had made the pro bowl. <a href="/wiki/Tramon_Williams" title="Tramon Williams">Tramon Williams</a> led the team with a career high 6 interceptions, while adding 326 punt return yards. Other pro bowl selections included safety <a href="/wiki/Nick_Collins" title="Nick Collins">Nick Collins</a> (4 interceptions and 70 combined tackles) and hard hitting 13-year veteran cornerback <a href="/wiki/Charles_Woodson" title="Charles Woodson">Charles Woodson</a>, who recorded 92 total tackles and forced five fumbles, while also intercepting two passes.</p>
<p>The Packers entered the Super Bowl never having trailed by more than 7 points at any point during the season — a feat that had never been accomplished during a complete season in the Super Bowl era. The last team to complete a season with this distinction was the <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Lions" title="Detroit Lions">Detroit Lions</a> in <a href="/wiki/1962_Detroit_Lions_season" title="1962 Detroit Lions season">1962</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> In the Super Bowl game itself, the Packers never trailed.</p>
<p>Of note, this was Green Bay's first Super Bowl against an AFC team that was not one of the "Original 8" <a href="/wiki/American_Football_League" title="American Football League">American Football League</a> franchises. The Packers had played Kansas City, Oakland, New England and Denver in their four previous Super Bowl match-ups, winning against all but Denver. The Steelers, like the Packers, predated the AFL's launch, having begun play in 1933 (12 years after the Packers joined the NFL after two years as an independent team), and moved to the AFC in <a href="/wiki/1970_NFL_season" title="1970 NFL season">1970</a> as a result of the <a href="/wiki/AFL%E2%80%93NFL_merger" title="AFL–NFL merger">AFL–NFL merger</a> to even out the two conferences.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Playoffs">Playoffs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_Bowl_XLV&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Playoffs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_NFL_playoffs" title="2010–11 NFL playoffs">2010–11 NFL playoffs</a></div>
<p>Pittsburgh advanced to the Super Bowl with two close wins in the playoffs. After a first-round bye, the Steelers defeated their division rival, the number 5 <a href="/wiki/2010_Baltimore_Ravens_season" title="2010 Baltimore Ravens season">Baltimore Ravens</a> 31–24, with <a href="/wiki/Ben_Roethlisberger" title="Ben Roethlisberger">Ben Roethlisberger</a>'s 58-yard completion to <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Brown" title="Antonio Brown">Antonio Brown</a> on third down and 19 setting up <a href="/wiki/Rashard_Mendenhall" title="Rashard Mendenhall">Rashard Mendenhall</a>'s game winning 2-yard touchdown run with 1:33 left in the game. Roethlisberger finished with 226 passing yards and two touchdowns, while the defense forced three turnovers and sacked Baltimore QB <a href="/wiki/Joe_Flacco" title="Joe Flacco">Joe Flacco</a> five times, three by <a href="/wiki/James_Harrison_(American_football)" title="James Harrison (American football)">James Harrison</a>.</p>
<p>Then the Steelers defeated the number 6 <a href="/wiki/2010_New_York_Jets_season" title="2010 New York Jets season">New York Jets</a> 24–19 in the AFC title game. Pittsburgh seemed to be in complete control at first, taking a 24–0 lead in the first half. New York quarterback <a href="/wiki/Mark_Sanchez" title="Mark Sanchez">Mark Sanchez</a> rallied his team back, cutting the score to 24–10 going into the fourth quarter. The Jets then drove to the Steelers 2-yard line on a 17-play drive, but the Pittsburgh defense made a key stand, keeping them out of the end zone on four consecutive plays near the goal-line to force a turnover. New York subsequently forced a safety and scored a touchdown with just over three minutes left, but Roethlisberger's 14-yard completions to Brown and <a href="/wiki/Heath_Miller" title="Heath Miller">Heath Miller</a> allowed Pittsburgh to hang on to the ball until time expired. Mendenhall finished with 121 rushing yards and a touchdown, along with 2 catches for 32 yards.</p>
<p>Green Bay started off their postseason with a 21–16 win over the number 3 <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Eagles" title="Philadelphia Eagles">Philadelphia Eagles</a> after <a href="/wiki/Tramon_Williams" title="Tramon Williams">Tramon Williams</a> intercepted a pass from <a href="/wiki/Michael_Vick" title="Michael Vick">Michael Vick</a> in the end zone with less than a minute left to play. <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Rodgers" title="Aaron Rodgers">Aaron Rodgers</a> threw for 180 yards and three touchdowns while <a href="/wiki/James_Starks" title="James Starks">James Starks</a>, who only rushed for 101 yards during the season, rushed for 123 yards in the game.</p>
<p>The Packers then went to Georgia, where the top-seeded 13–3 <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons" title="Atlanta Falcons">Atlanta Falcons</a> were waiting. Although the Falcons took advantage of an early turnover and a kick return touchdown to build a 14–7 lead, Green Bay quickly buried the Falcons with 35 straight points. By the end of the first half, the Packers held a 28–14 lead, and went on to win comfortably, 48–21. Rodgers was nearly perfect, completing 31 of 36 passes for 366 yards and three touchdowns, while adding another score on the ground. <a href="/wiki/Jordy_Nelson" title="Jordy Nelson">Jordy Nelson</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_Jones_(wide_receiver)" title="James Jones (wide receiver)">James Jones</a> both had touchdown catches, while <a href="/wiki/John_Kuhn" title="John Kuhn">John Kuhn</a> added scores by air and ground and Tramon Williams returned one of his two interceptions 70 yards for a touchdown. Green Bay's special teams unit never had to punt the ball, while <a href="/wiki/Mason_Crosby" title="Mason Crosby">Mason Crosby</a> contributed two field goals.</p>
<p>Green Bay next faced the number 2 <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Bears" title="Chicago Bears">Chicago Bears</a> in the NFC championship game, beating them 21–14. This time Rodgers had a rougher day than his previous two games, throwing no touchdown passes and being intercepted twice. But he still threw for 244 yards and scored a 1-yard touchdown run, while Starks added 74 rushing yards, including a touchdown run in the second quarter. Meanwhile, Green Bay's defense knocked Chicago quarterback <a href="/wiki/Jay_Cutler_(American_football)" title="Jay Cutler (American football)">Jay Cutler</a> out of the game and intercepted three passes, one of which was returned 18 yards for a touchdown by <a href="/wiki/B._J._Raji" title="B. J. Raji">B. J. Raji</a>. The other two were made by rookie <a href="/wiki/Sam_Shields" title="Sam Shields">Sam Shields</a>, who recorded his second interception near his own end zone with 37 seconds left to put the game away.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Super_Bowl_pregame_notes">Super Bowl pregame notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_Bowl_XLV&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Super Bowl pregame notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:American_Sign_Language_Interpreter.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/American_Sign_Language_Interpreter.jpg/250px-American_Sign_Language_Interpreter.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/American_Sign_Language_Interpreter.jpg/375px-American_Sign_Language_Interpreter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/American_Sign_Language_Interpreter.jpg/500px-American_Sign_Language_Interpreter.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:American_Sign_Language_Interpreter.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An <a href="/wiki/American_Sign_Language" title="American Sign Language">American Sign Language</a> interpreter in the <a href="/wiki/Joe_Greene_(American_football)" title="Joe Greene (American football)">Joe Greene</a> jersey appearing at a rally for the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Steelers" title="Pittsburgh Steelers">Pittsburgh Steelers</a> prior to Super Bowl XLV.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Both teams are known to have sizable fanbases that often travel to away games, largely due to the home games themselves having <a href="/wiki/NFL_season_ticket_waiting_lists" title="NFL season ticket waiting lists">decades-long waiting lists</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> In August 2008, <a href="/wiki/ESPN.com" title="ESPN.com">ESPN.com</a> ranked the two teams tied as having the best fans in the NFL.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a>'s own <a href="/wiki/John_Clayton_(sportswriter)" title="John Clayton (sportswriter)">John Clayton</a>, a Pittsburgh native, broke the tie in favor of the Steelers.</p>
<p>As the Packers were the designated home team in the annual rotation between AFC and NFC teams, the team elected to wear their green jerseys.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Although both teams are known to wear their colored jerseys at home and have rarely worn white at home (the Packers wore white at home for two games in 1989), the Packers decision contrasted with the Steelers decision as the home team in <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XL" title="Super Bowl XL">Super Bowl XL</a> to wear white jerseys. Both the <a href="/wiki/2005_Pittsburgh_Steelers_season" title="2005 Pittsburgh Steelers season">2005 Steelers</a> and 2010 Packers were number 6 seeded teams when they reached the Super Bowl, forcing them to play all of their postseason games on the road and wearing their respective white jerseys in those games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Retractable_roof" title="Retractable roof">retractable roof</a> at Cowboys Stadium was closed for the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>A severe <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/January_31_%E2%80%93_February_2,_2011_North_American_winter_storm" title="January 31 – February 2, 2011 North American winter storm">winter storm</a> blanketed the Dallas-Fort Worth area in hard ice and snow the week before the game, threatening to disrupt game preparations. Snow fell from the roof of Cowboys Stadium's East end on February 4, injuring six people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Over 3,000 tickets were sold to watch the game in the stadium's East Plaza, which experienced the falling ice tragedy earlier in the week. However, the snow had melted by game time and fans who paid $200 per ticket were allowed to watch the game outside Cowboys Stadium, in the open air, as the weather turned from sleet to sun.</p>
<p>Since the Steelers and Packers were two of the six teams that did not have <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cheerleader" title="Cheerleader">cheerleaders</a> during the 2010 NFL season (the others being the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Bears" title="Chicago Bears">Chicago Bears</a>, <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Lions" title="Detroit Lions">Detroit Lions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Browns" title="Cleveland Browns">Cleveland Browns</a>, and <a href="/wiki/New_York_Giants" title="New York Giants">New York Giants</a>), this marked the first Super Bowl without cheerleaders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>Packers lineman, <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Bulaga" title="Bryan Bulaga">Bryan Bulaga</a>, became the youngest player to start in a Super Bowl, at the age of 21 years and 322 days old. Steelers center <a href="/wiki/Maurkice_Pouncey" title="Maurkice Pouncey">Maurkice Pouncey</a> would have been the youngest player (21 years, 197 days), but he could not play because of a high ankle sprain.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Possible_Presidential_appearance">Possible Presidential appearance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_Bowl_XLV&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Possible Presidential appearance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>During a press conference on January 19, 2011, President <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Obama" title="Obama">Obama</a> (a longtime <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Bears" title="Chicago Bears">Chicago Bears</a> fan) said he would attend Super Bowl XLV if Chicago defeated <a href="/wiki/Green_Bay_Packers" title="Green Bay Packers">Green Bay</a>, saying "If Chicago wins, I’m going no doubt".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Chicago ended up losing the NFC Championship game a few days later on January 23 to Green Bay 21–14. In a post-game locker-room speech by Green Bay Packers corner <a href="/wiki/Charles_Woodson" title="Charles Woodson">Charles Woodson</a> he poked fun at the President's comment saying "The President don't want to come watch us at the Super Bowl, guess what? We'll go see him" (implying that Green Bay would win the Super Bowl and visit the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> as the winning team does each year; a statement that would come true). Woodson then broke the Packers meeting with a team cheer of "White House!".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> On January 26 President Obama visited Green Bay and was greeted by Mayor <a href="/wiki/Jim_Schmitt" title="Jim Schmitt">Jim Schmitt</a> and Wisconsin Governor <a href="/wiki/Scott_Walker_(politician)" title="Scott Walker (politician)">Scott Walker</a> who presented the President with two Green Bay Packers Jerseys. The first had Obama's name on the back with the number 1 and the second was an autographed Charles Woodson jersey with the message "See you at the White House. Go Packers!" written on the back by Woodson.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>On August 12, 2011, Woodson's promise came true and Packers visited the White House and met with President Obama. Their visit was delayed because of the NFL lockout and took place a day before the Packers first preseason game against the <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Browns" title="Cleveland Browns">Cleveland Browns</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> President Obama was presented with a Packers jersey with the number 1 and the words Commander-In-Chief on the back. He was also presented with a stock share of the Packers organization, thus making him a part owner of the Packers. When Obama jokingly asked if this meant he could trade Aaron Rodgers to the Bears, Woodson responded that Obama was just "a minority owner."</p>
<p>Obama, who is also a <a href="/wiki/Steeler_Nation" title="Steeler Nation">Steelers fan</a> and considers the team to be his second-favorite after the Bears, openly supported the Steelers two years earlier in <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLIII" title="Super Bowl XLIII">Super Bowl XLIII</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Rooney_family" title="Rooney family">Rooney family</a> helped with his <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2008" title="United States presidential election, 2008">campaigning work</a> and later appointed Steelers chairman <a href="/wiki/Dan_Rooney" title="Dan Rooney">Dan Rooney</a>, an ethnic <a href="/wiki/Irish_Catholic" title="Irish Catholic">Irish Catholic</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Ambassador_to_Ireland" title="United States Ambassador to Ireland">U.S. Ambassador to Ireland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> He did not attend the game; instead, he hosted a 100-person Super Bowl party at the White House. Attendees included his family, elected leaders from Pennsylvania and Wisconsin, DNC member Andres Lopez of Puerto Rico, <a href="/wiki/Buffalo,_New_York" title="Buffalo, New York">Buffalo, New York</a> mayor <a href="/wiki/Byron_Brown" title="Byron Brown">Byron Brown</a>, Buffalo deputy mayor Steve Casey, <a href="/wiki/Newark,_New_Jersey" title="Newark, New Jersey">Newark, New Jersey</a> mayor <a href="/wiki/Cory_Booker" title="Cory Booker">Cory Booker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Lopez" title="Jennifer Lopez">Jennifer Lopez</a> and her husband <a href="/wiki/Marc_Anthony" title="Marc Anthony">Marc Anthony</a>, both actors/singers, <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> columnist <a href="/wiki/Michael_Wilbon" title="Michael Wilbon">Michael Wilbon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tony_Kornheiser" title="Tony Kornheiser">Tony Kornheiser</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although the sitting president did not attend the game, former president and former Texas governor <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> was present, along with his wife <a href="/wiki/Laura_Bush" title="Laura Bush">Laura</a> and former <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/Condoleezza_Rice" title="Condoleezza Rice">Condoleezza Rice</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_commemoration">Local commemoration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_Bowl_XLV&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Local commemoration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>From June 15, 2010, through February 6, 2011, the 30-mile section of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_30_in_Texas" title="Interstate 30 in Texas">Interstate 30</a> between Dallas and Fort Worth along which <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Stadium" title="AT&amp;T Stadium">Cowboys Stadium</a> is situated had been temporarily designated as the "Tom Landry Super Bowl Highway" in commemoration of Super Bowl XLV.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-do100610_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-do100610-28">[28]</a></sup> The former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dallas-Fort_Worth_Turnpike" title="Dallas-Fort Worth Turnpike">Dallas-Fort Worth Turnpike</a> is normally known as the "Tom Landry Highway" in honor of former <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Cowboys" title="Dallas Cowboys">Dallas Cowboys</a> coach <a href="/wiki/Tom_Landry" title="Tom Landry">Tom Landry</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-do100610_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-do100610-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Logo">Logo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_Bowl_XLV&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Logo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>While past Super Bowl games used their own unique logo designs that changed yearly, Super Bowl XLV introduced a new standard design for the game's logo. It incorporates an image of the <a href="/wiki/Vince_Lombardi_Trophy" title="Vince Lombardi Trophy">Vince Lombardi Trophy</a> sitting atop the traditional <a href="/wiki/Roman_numerals" title="Roman numerals">Roman numerals</a> used to denote each edition, with a stylized image of the host stadium shown in the background. It was introduced as part of a unification of branding across the NFL's post-season games, which also saw the redesign of the conference championship trophies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-espn-standardlogo_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-espn-standardlogo-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>The only changes made to the logo for future Super Bowls will be to change the number and the stadium depicted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-espn-standardlogo_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-espn-standardlogo-30">[30]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_50" title="Super Bowl 50">Super Bowl 50</a> deviated slightly from the standard design to emphasize the game's "golden anniversary", featuring the number "50" in large gold numbering on each side of the trophy rather than below it in Roman numerals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESPN20140604_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN20140604-31">[31]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_LI" title="Super Bowl LI">Super Bowl LI</a> returned to using Roman numerals, but retained the modified layout used by the Super Bowl 50 logo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Broadcasting">Broadcasting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_Bowl_XLV&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Broadcasting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_Bowl_XLV&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_Bowl_XLV&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Fox_NFL" title="Fox NFL">Fox Sports</a> televised the game in the United States, with <a href="/wiki/Joe_Buck" title="Joe Buck">Joe Buck</a> as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Play-by-play" title="Play-by-play">play-by-play</a> announcer and <a href="/wiki/Troy_Aikman" title="Troy Aikman">Troy Aikman</a>, himself a three-time Super Bowl winner as a <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Cowboys" title="Dallas Cowboys">Dallas Cowboys</a> quarterback, as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Color_analyst" title="Color analyst">color analyst</a>. <a href="/wiki/Mike_Pereira" title="Mike Pereira">Mike Pereira</a> joined Buck and Aikman in the broadcast booth to comment on <a href="/wiki/Instant_replay_in_American_and_Canadian_football" title="Instant replay in American and Canadian football">instant replay</a> reviews,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Pam_Oliver" title="Pam Oliver">Pam Oliver</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Myers" title="Chris Myers">Chris Myers</a> served as <a href="/wiki/Sideline_reporter" title="Sideline reporter">sideline reporters</a>. The pre-game show featured the <i><a href="/wiki/Fox_NFL_Sunday" title="Fox NFL Sunday">Fox NFL Sunday</a></i> crew of host <a href="/wiki/Curt_Menefee" title="Curt Menefee">Curt Menefee</a> and a group of analysts with extensive Super Bowl experiences of their own: <a href="/wiki/Terry_Bradshaw" title="Terry Bradshaw">Terry Bradshaw</a> (4 time Super Bowl winning QB with the Pittsburgh Steelers), <a href="/wiki/Howie_Long" title="Howie Long">Howie Long</a> (one-time Super Bowl winning defensive end with the then-Los Angeles Raiders), <a href="/wiki/Michael_Strahan" title="Michael Strahan">Michael Strahan</a> (one-time Super Bowl winning defensive end with the NY Giants) and <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Johnson_(American_football_coach)" title="Jimmy Johnson (American football coach)">Jimmy Johnson</a> (two-time Super Bowl winning head coach with the Cowboys). They were joined by a variety of other commentators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>Five days prior to the game, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Immigration_and_Customs_Enforcement" title="U.S. Immigration and Customs Enforcement">Immigration and Customs Enforcement</a>, along with the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Attorney_for_the_Southern_District_of_New_York" title="United States Attorney for the Southern District of New York">United States Attorney for the Southern District of New York</a>, seized and shut down several websites that had provided access to pirated <a href="/wiki/Internet_television" title="Internet television">Internet television</a> feeds of NFL games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>With an average US audience of 111 million viewers, this was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_most-watched_television_broadcasts#United_States" title="List of most-watched television broadcasts">most-watched</a> Super Bowl as well as the most-watched program of any kind in American television history, beating the previous record of 106.5 million viewers for <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLIV" title="Super Bowl XLIV">Super Bowl XLIV</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> An estimated 162.9 million total viewers watched all or part of the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seidman1987_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-seidman1987-4">[4]</a></sup> The game drew a national household <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nielsen_rating" title="Nielsen rating">Nielsen rating</a> of 46.0 and a 69 share. It drew a 59.7 local rating in both Milwaukee (<a href="/wiki/WITI_(TV)" title="WITI (TV)">WITI</a>) and Pittsburgh (<a href="/wiki/WPGH-TV" title="WPGH-TV">WPGH</a>), the second-highest local rating for a Super Bowl after the 63.0 that <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XX" title="Super Bowl XX">Super Bowl XX</a> drew in Chicago. In the host market of Dallas-Fort Worth (<a href="/wiki/KDFW" title="KDFW">KDFW</a>), the game drew a 53.7 rating.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Steelers also became the second team to appear on Super Bowls on all four major networks, after the <a href="/wiki/Denver_Broncos" title="Denver Broncos">Denver Broncos</a>. The Steelers appeared previously on four <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>-aired Super Bowls (<a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_IX" title="Super Bowl IX">IX</a>, <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XIII" title="Super Bowl XIII">XIII</a>, <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXX" title="Super Bowl XXX">XXX</a>, <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLIII" title="Super Bowl XLIII">XLIII</a>), two <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a>-aired Super Bowls (<a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_X" title="Super Bowl X">X</a>, <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XIV" title="Super Bowl XIV">XIV</a>), and one <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a>-aired Super Bowl (<a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XL" title="Super Bowl XL">XL</a>).</p>
<p>Fox's <a href="/wiki/List_of_Super_Bowl_lead-out_programs" title="List of Super Bowl lead-out programs">lead-out program</a> was an episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Glee_(TV_series)" title="Glee (TV series)">Glee</a></i> titled "<a href="/wiki/The_Sue_Sylvester_Shuffle" title="The Sue Sylvester Shuffle">The Sue Sylvester Shuffle</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercials">Commercials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_Bowl_XLV&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Commercials">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>By September 15, 2010, Fox had sold 90% of all available slots; all slots were completely sold out by October. The price of an advertisement began at US$3,000,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-apads_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-apads-5">[5]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pepsi-Cola" title="Pepsi-Cola">Pepsi-Cola</a> returned after a one-year retreat with three ads for their <a href="/wiki/Pepsi_Max" title="Pepsi Max">Pepsi Max</a> drink, which has been named as the official soft drink of the NFL. Pepsi's <a href="/wiki/Frito-Lay" title="Frito-Lay">Frito-Lay</a> brand also advertised <a href="/wiki/Doritos" title="Doritos">Doritos</a>. Both brands had their advertisements created by web users as part of the annual <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USA_Today_Super_Bowl_Ad_Meter" title="USA Today Super Bowl Ad Meter">USA Today Super Bowl Ad Meter</a> contest, which offers a prize of <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US $</a>5 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> In addition, regular purchasers <a href="/wiki/Anheuser-Busch_InBev" title="Anheuser-Busch InBev">Anheuser-Busch InBev</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Go_Daddy" title="Go Daddy">GoDaddy.com</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CareerBuilder.com" title="CareerBuilder.com">CareerBuilder.com</a>, and <a href="/wiki/E-Trade" title="E-Trade">E*TRADE</a> purchased advertisements; InBev advertised <a href="/wiki/Stella_Artois" title="Stella Artois">Stella Artois</a> imported beer for the first time in the Super Bowl in addition to its usual <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Budweiser_(Anheuser-Busch)" title="Budweiser (Anheuser-Busch)">Budweiser</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bud_Light" title="Bud Light">Bud Light</a> advertisements. <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Motor_Company" title="Hyundai Motor Company">Hyundai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz" title="Mercedes-Benz">Mercedes-Benz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Audi" title="Audi">Audi</a> also advertised,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-apads_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-apads-5">[5]</a></sup> as did <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a>, who returned for the first time since their bankruptcy with advertisements for the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet" title="Chevrolet">Chevrolet</a> <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Cruze" title="Chevrolet Cruze">Cruze</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Camaro" title="Chevrolet Camaro">Camaro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Silverado" title="Chevrolet Silverado">Silverado</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Volt" title="Chevrolet Volt">Volt</a>. <a href="/wiki/Chrysler" title="Chrysler">Chrysler</a> purchased a 2-minute-long advertisement for its <a href="/wiki/Chrysler_200" title="Chrysler 200">Chrysler 200</a> featuring <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>.</p>
<p>Advertisements for 15 films were shown during the Pre-Game, Game, and Post-Game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="International_telecasts">International telecasts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_Bowl_XLV&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: International telecasts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>NFL International provided television coverage for viewers outside of North America, with <a href="/wiki/Bob_Papa" title="Bob Papa">Bob Papa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joe_Theismann" title="Joe Theismann">Joe Theismann</a> calling the English language feed. The game was shown live on the following channels:</p>
<ul>
<li><b>Asia</b>: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/All_Sports_Network" title="All Sports Network">All Sports Network</a>.
<ul>
<li><b><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span>China</b>: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DragonTV" title="DragonTV">DragonTV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Media_Group" title="Shanghai Media Group">G-Sports</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guangdong_TV" title="Guangdong TV">GDTV Sports</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beijing_Television" title="Beijing Television">BTV Sports</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CNTV" title="CNTV">CNTV 5+</a> (online), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sina.com" title="Sina.com">Sina TV</a> (online), <a href="/wiki/QQLive" title="QQLive">QQLive</a> (online), .</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><b><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="1280" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b9/Flag_of_Australia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Australia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b9/Flag_of_Australia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Australia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b9/Flag_of_Australia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Australia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span>Australia</b>: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/One_HD" title="One HD">One HD</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Network_Ten" title="Network Ten">Network Ten</a>. In addition it was also broadcast live on <a href="/wiki/ESPN_Australia" title="ESPN Australia">ESPN Australia</a>.</li>
<li><b><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="1000" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/23px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/35px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/46px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span>Canada</b>: <a href="/wiki/CTV_Television_Network" title="CTV Television Network">CTV</a> in English (using the FOX feed) and <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9seau_des_sports" title="Réseau des sports">RDS</a> in French. As in past years, CTV exercised its <a href="/wiki/Simultaneous_substitution" title="Simultaneous substitution">simultaneous substitution</a> rights over American stations carrying the game on Canadian cable and satellite providers.</li>
<li><b><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="540" data-file-width="810" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/23px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/35px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/45px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a></b>: <a href="/wiki/ESPN_America" title="ESPN America">ESPN America</a>, in addition to the following local broadcasters:
<ul>
<li><b><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_Austria.svg/23px-Flag_of_Austria.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_Austria.svg/35px-Flag_of_Austria.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_Austria.svg/45px-Flag_of_Austria.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a></b>: <a href="/wiki/Puls_4" title="Puls 4">Puls 4</a>.</li>
<li><b><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="450" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg/45px-Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span>Belgium</b>: <a href="/wiki/Liberty_Global" title="Liberty Global">Prime Sport</a>, <a href="/wiki/BeTV_(Belgium)" title="BeTV (Belgium)">BeTV</a>.</li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio">Radio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_Bowl_XLV&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Radio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NFL_on_Westwood_One" title="NFL on Westwood One">Westwood One</a> broadcast Super Bowl XLV across the United States and Canada, with play-by-play announcer <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Harlan" title="Kevin Harlan">Kevin Harlan</a> (calling his first Super Bowl for the network) and color analyst <a href="/wiki/Boomer_Esiason" title="Boomer Esiason">Boomer Esiason</a>. <a href="/wiki/Univision_Radio" title="Univision Radio">Univision Radio</a> carried a Spanish language feed for its stations throughout the US. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flagship_(radio)" title="Flagship (radio)">flagship stations</a> for each team also carried the game with their respective local announcers:</p>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Packers_Radio_Network" title="Packers Radio Network">Packers Radio Network</a> via <a href="/wiki/WTAQ" title="WTAQ">WTAQ</a>, WTAQ-FM and <a href="/wiki/WIXX" title="WIXX">WIXX</a> in Green Bay and <a href="/wiki/WTMJ_(AM)" title="WTMJ (AM)">WTMJ</a> in Milwaukee, with <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Larrivee" title="Wayne Larrivee">Wayne Larrivee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Larry_McCarren" title="Larry McCarren">Larry McCarren</a> announcing.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Steelers_Radio_Network" title="Pittsburgh Steelers Radio Network">Pittsburgh Steelers Radio Network</a> via <a href="/wiki/WDVE" title="WDVE">WDVE</a> and <a href="/wiki/WBGG_(AM)" title="WBGG (AM)">WBGG</a> in Pittsburgh, with <a href="/wiki/Bill_Hillgrove" title="Bill Hillgrove">Bill Hillgrove</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tunch_Ilkin" title="Tunch Ilkin">Tunch Ilkin</a> announcing.</li>
</ul>
<p>In the United Kingdom, <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_5_Live" title="BBC Radio 5 Live">BBC Radio 5 Live</a> carried radio coverage with Darren Fletcher and <a href="/wiki/Greg_Brady_(broadcaster)" title="Greg Brady (broadcaster)">Greg Brady</a> announcing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sirius_XM_Satellite_Radio" title="Sirius XM Satellite Radio">Sirius XM Satellite Radio</a> carried 14 feeds in ten languages to <a href="/wiki/Sirius_Satellite_Radio" title="Sirius Satellite Radio">Sirius</a> subscribers, as well as to <a href="/wiki/XM_Satellite_Radio" title="XM Satellite Radio">XM</a> subscribers with the "Best of Sirius" package.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> In addition to the Westwood One and local team broadcasts, Sirius carried the following international feeds:</p>
<ul>

<li><b><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span>Netherlands</b>: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prime_Televisie" title="Prime Televisie">Prime Sport</a> (Dutch)</li>
<li><b><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span>Russia</b>: <a href="/wiki/NTV_Plus" title="NTV Plus">NTV Plus</a> (Russian)</li>
<li><b><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="750" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/23px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/35px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/45px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span>Spain</b>: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canal%2B_(Spain)" title="Canal+ (Spain)">Canal+ Spain</a> (Spanish)</li>
<li><b><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span>United Kingdom</b>: <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_5_Live" title="BBC Radio 5 Live">BBC Radio 5 Live</a> (English)</li>
</ul>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FieldPass" title="FieldPass">FieldPass</a>, the subscription Internet radio service provided by the league at NFL.com, also carried most of these feeds. Due to contractual restrictions, only Sirius XM and FieldPass were permitted to carry the local team broadcasts along with WTAQ, WIXX, WTMJ, WDVE and WBGG, with the teams' other network radio affiliates instead airing the Westwood One feed.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Attendance">Attendance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_Bowl_XLV&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Attendance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Stadium" title="AT&amp;T Stadium">Cowboys Stadium</a> installed 15,000 temporary seats and utilized its standing room to increase its capacity to over 105,000 fans. If the stadium had been filled to capacity (its record for an NFL game is 105,121 spectators), it would have set a record for Super Bowl attendance, breaking the previous record of 103,985 fans for <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XIV" title="Super Bowl XIV">Super Bowl XIV</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Rose_Bowl_(stadium)" title="Rose Bowl (stadium)">Rose Bowl</a>; however the actual attendance of 103,219<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> fell 766 fans short. League officials had indicated that they would also count spectators watching the game on large television screens from outside the stadium in the tally, which generally is not allowed in official attendance counts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>Due to numerous delays, 1,250 temporary seats weren't ready in time for the game. According to a police officer standing near the affected area, the seats hadn't been installed in time for the fire marshal to inspect them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> The NFL scrambled almost until kickoff to find replacement seats. Eventually, 850 fans in four sections were relocated, while 400 fans in two sections were given a refund equivalent to three times the face value of their ticket.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> The latter set of fans were later offered the chance to watch the game on monitors in the North Field Club behind the Steelers bench, but would still get the triple refund. Some of these fans were still upset, since they had spent thousands on airfare and hotels. NFL spokesman Brian McCarthy said that when the league decided to relocate the 850 fans, it lost any shot of setting the attendance record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>The NFL subsequently offered affected fans a ticket to the next Super Bowl in addition to the refund. It also offered fans the option of a ticket to any future Super Bowl, along with round-trip airfare and hotel accommodations. However, this wasn't enough to mollify several fans, who on February 9 filed a $5 million <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Class-action_lawsuit" title="Class-action lawsuit">class-action lawsuit</a> against the NFL, the Cowboys and Jones. In addition to Steelers and Packers fans left without seats, the suit includes Cowboys fans who paid $100,000 for <a href="/wiki/Personal_seat_license" title="Personal seat license">personal seat licenses</a>, only to have to watch the Super Bowl in metal folding chairs without a view of the stadium's giant video replay board.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> The NFL at first offered $2,400 to fans who did not receive a replacement seat, but later offered tickets to a future Super Bowl with airfare and hotels included.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>Not all of the fans accepted the NFL's settlement offer, so the case went to trial. The final outcome of the lawsuit was a finding for the plaintiffs against the NFL in the matter of breach of contract, and not liable for fraudulent inducement. The Cowboys and Jerry Jones were dismissed as parties to the lawsuit since the plaintiffs' contracts were solely with the NFL. The plaintiffs were awarded between $5,600 and $22,000 depending on the value of their tickets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Entertainment_and_other_ceremonies">Entertainment and other ceremonies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_Bowl_XLV&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Entertainment and other ceremonies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pregame">Pregame</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_Bowl_XLV&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Pregame">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Keith_Urban" title="Keith Urban">Keith Urban</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maroon_5" title="Maroon 5">Maroon 5</a> performed during the pregame.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-apmusic_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-apmusic-52">[52]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Texas_Christian_University" title="Texas Christian University">Texas Christian University</a> Horned Frog Marching Band also performed during the pregame show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcusuperbowl_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-tcusuperbowl-53">[53]</a></sup> 22-year-old Candice Villesca of <a href="/wiki/Lewisville,_Texas" title="Lewisville, Texas">Lewisville, Texas</a> performed the national anthem and "America the Beautiful" in <a href="/wiki/American_Sign_Language" title="American Sign Language">American Sign Language</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lea_Michele" title="Lea Michele">Lea Michele</a> performed "<a href="/wiki/America_the_Beautiful" title="America the Beautiful">America the Beautiful</a>"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aguilera_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Aguilera-55">[55]</a></sup> supported by the Air Force <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tops_in_Blue" title="Tops in Blue">Tops in Blue</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Pop singer <a href="/wiki/Christina_Aguilera" title="Christina Aguilera">Christina Aguilera</a> sang the <a href="/wiki/The_Star-Spangled_Banner" title="The Star-Spangled Banner">national anthem</a>, but performed the wrong lyrics for the fourth line of the song,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> later issuing an apology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>The coin toss ceremony was the first to commemorate two anniversaries—the 25th anniversary of <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XX" title="Super Bowl XX">Super Bowl XX</a> and 15th of <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXX" title="Super Bowl XXX">Super Bowl XXX</a>, which marked the <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Cowboys" title="Dallas Cowboys">Dallas Cowboys</a>' most recent Super Bowl championship. In honor of those occasions, Super Bowl XX MVP <a href="/wiki/Richard_Dent" title="Richard Dent">Richard Dent</a> and former Dallas Cowboys defensive back <a href="/wiki/Deion_Sanders" title="Deion Sanders">Deion Sanders</a>, both of whom were inducted into the Pro Football Hall of Fame in 2011, joined the ceremonies. They were joined by fellow Pro Football Hall of Fame inductees and past Super Bowl participants <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Faulk" title="Marshall Faulk">Marshall Faulk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Hanburger" title="Chris Hanburger">Chris Hanburger</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shannon_Sharpe" title="Shannon Sharpe">Shannon Sharpe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Halftime">Halftime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_Bowl_XLV&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Halftime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/The_Black_Eyed_Peas" title="The Black Eyed Peas">The Black Eyed Peas</a> performed a medley of their greatest hits: "<a href="/wiki/I_Gotta_Feeling" title="I Gotta Feeling">I Gotta Feeling</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Boom_Boom_Pow" title="Boom Boom Pow">Boom Boom Pow</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Pump_It" title="Pump It">Pump It</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Time_(Dirty_Bit)" title="The Time (Dirty Bit)">The Time (Dirty Bit)</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Let%27s_Get_It_Started" title="Let's Get It Started">Let's Get It Started</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/Where_Is_the_Love%3F" title="Where Is the Love?">Where Is the Love?</a>" <a href="/wiki/Slash_(musician)" title="Slash (musician)">Slash</a> made a guest appearance, performing "<a href="/wiki/Sweet_Child_o%27_Mine" title="Sweet Child o' Mine">Sweet Child o' Mine</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Fergie_(singer)" title="Fergie (singer)">Fergie</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Usher_(singer)" title="Usher (singer)">Usher</a> made an appearance to perform his song "<a href="/wiki/OMG_(song)" title="OMG (song)">OMG</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Will.i.am" title="Will.i.am">will.i.am</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-apmusic_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-apmusic-52">[52]</a></sup> The show also displayed a long list of other performers, including Prairie View A&amp;M University's "Marching Storm" Band.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Country_music" title="Country music">Country music</a> was originally in the planning until the Black Eyed Peas agreed to perform.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Game_summary">Game summary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_Bowl_XLV&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Game summary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>After the first three drives of the game ended with punts, Green Bay opened up the scoring with <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Rodgers" title="Aaron Rodgers">Aaron Rodgers</a>'s 29-yard touchdown pass to <a href="/wiki/Jordy_Nelson" title="Jordy Nelson">Jordy Nelson</a>, who managed to pull slightly ahead of cornerback <a href="/wiki/William_Gay_(cornerback)" title="William Gay (cornerback)">William Gay</a> enough to make a leaping catch and fall into the end zone. Then on the first play after the ensuing kickoff, quarterback <a href="/wiki/Ben_Roethlisberger" title="Ben Roethlisberger">Ben Roethlisberger</a> was hit by <a href="/wiki/Howard_Green" title="Howard Green">Howard Green</a> as he threw a pass, causing the ball to go well short of his intended target near the left sideline where it was intercepted by <a href="/wiki/Nick_Collins" title="Nick Collins">Nick Collins</a> and returned 37 yards for a touchdown, giving Green Bay a 14–0 lead. This score continued the unbeaten streak of Super Bowl victories recorded by teams scoring on an interception runback, improving to 11–0 in such games. It was also the third consecutive Super Bowl with an interception return for a touchdown, as well as the eighth such score in the last ten Super Bowls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> The Packers also tied the <a href="/wiki/1973_Miami_Dolphins_season" title="1973 Miami Dolphins season">Miami Dolphins'</a> record which still stands for the largest Super Bowl lead (14 points) at the end of the first quarter, set in <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_VIII" title="Super Bowl VIII">Super Bowl VIII</a> against the <a href="/wiki/1973_Minnesota_Vikings_season" title="1973 Minnesota Vikings season">Minnesota Vikings</a> and later tied by the <a href="/wiki/1980_Oakland_Raiders_season" title="1980 Oakland Raiders season">Oakland Raiders</a> against the <a href="/wiki/1980_Philadelphia_Eagles_season" title="1980 Philadelphia Eagles season">Philadelphia Eagles</a> in <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XV" title="Super Bowl XV">Super Bowl XV</a>.</p>
<p>This time Pittsburgh managed to respond, driving 49 yards in 13 plays including Roethlisberger's 18-yard run on 3rd down and 9. <a href="/wiki/Shaun_Suisham" title="Shaun Suisham">Shaun Suisham</a> finished the drive with a 33-yard field goal to cut the score to 14–3. Then after forcing a punt, the Steelers drove to midfield, but turned the ball over again when Roethlisberger's pass was intercepted by defensive back <a href="/wiki/Jarrett_Bush" title="Jarrett Bush">Jarrett Bush</a> at the 47. Then Rodgers led the Packers to another score, completing two passes for 20 yards before <a href="/wiki/James_Starks" title="James Starks">James Starks</a>'s 12-yard run moved the ball to the 21-yard line. On the next play, Green Bay increased their lead to 21–3 with Rodgers' 21-yard touchdown pass to <a href="/wiki/Greg_Jennings" title="Greg Jennings">Greg Jennings</a>. Taking the ball back with 2:24 left in the second quarter, Roethlisberger made a 37-yard completion to <a href="/wiki/Antwaan_Randle_El" title="Antwaan Randle El">Antwaan Randle El</a> on their first play. After that, receiver <a href="/wiki/Hines_Ward" title="Hines Ward">Hines Ward</a> caught 3 passes for 39 yards on the drive, the last one an 8-yard touchdown catch with 37 seconds left in the half, making the score 21–10 at halftime. This was the fourth time in their four 2011 postseason games that the Packers finished the first half with a lead of at least 11 points. The first half had taken a heavy toll on both teams. The Steelers lost receiver <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Sanders" title="Emmanuel Sanders">Emmanuel Sanders</a> to injury, while the Packers lost receiver <a href="/wiki/Donald_Driver" title="Donald Driver">Donald Driver</a> along with defensive backs <a href="/wiki/Charles_Woodson" title="Charles Woodson">Charles Woodson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sam_Shields" title="Sam Shields">Sam Shields</a>. Shields would be the only player among them who would return. The Black Eyed Peas played at halftime.</p>
<p>Pittsburgh's defense forced Green Bay to punt on the first drive of the second half, and got the ball at midfield after a facemask call on <a href="/wiki/Tom_Crabtree" title="Tom Crabtree">Tom Crabtree</a> while tackling <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Brown" title="Antonio Brown">Antonio Brown</a> on the punt return. The offense then scored in five plays (all runs). First <a href="/wiki/Rashard_Mendenhall" title="Rashard Mendenhall">Rashard Mendenhall</a> broke free along with right sideline for a 17-yard run, then <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Redman" title="Isaac Redman">Isaac Redman</a> rushed for 3 yards, and Roethlisberger ran for 6, bringing up third down and 1. On the next play, Redman tried to run up the middle, but was held up at the line, so he backed away and ran to the outside for a 16-yard gain to the 8-yard line. Then Mendenhall scored an 8-yard touchdown run on the next play, making the score 21–17. After forcing a punt, Pittsburgh mounted a drive to the Packers 29-yard line, but Green Bay's defense made a stand. First Roethlisberger's pass was batted down behind the line by linebacker <a href="/wiki/Clay_Matthews_III" title="Clay Matthews III">Clay Matthews</a>, then Roethlisberger tried a <a href="/wiki/Screen_pass" title="Screen pass">screen pass</a> to tight end <a href="/wiki/Heath_Miller" title="Heath Miller">Heath Miller</a>, but <a href="/wiki/Desmond_Bishop" title="Desmond Bishop">Desmond Bishop</a> tackled him for a 3-yard loss. Then on third down <a href="/wiki/Frank_Zombo" title="Frank Zombo">Frank Zombo</a> sacked Roethlisberger on the 34, and Suisham's ensuing 52-yard field goal attempt sailed wide left.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the first play of the fourth quarter, the Steelers lost their third turnover of the game when Mendenhall fumbled the ball while being tackled behind the line by Matthews and <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Pickett" title="Ryan Pickett">Ryan Pickett</a>. Bishop recovered the ball and returned it 7 yards to the Packers 45. Five plays later on third down and 10, Rodgers completed a 38-yard pass to Nelson at the Steelers 2-yard line. Pittsburgh linebacker <a href="/wiki/LaMarr_Woodley" title="LaMarr Woodley">LaMarr Woodley</a> sacked Rodgers for a 6-yard loss on the next play, but Rodgers threw an 8-yard touchdown pass to Jennings after that, increasing the Packers lead to 28–17. Roethlisberger led the Steelers right back with 6 of 7 completions. After a 9-yard pass to tight end <a href="/wiki/Matt_Spaeth" title="Matt Spaeth">Matt Spaeth</a>, he threw three completions to receiver <a href="/wiki/Mike_Wallace_(American_football)" title="Mike Wallace (American football)">Mike Wallace</a> for 27 yards to the Green Bay 40-yard line. Then after a 15-yard completion to Ward, he finished the drive with a 25-yard touchdown pass to Wallace. On the two-point conversion play, Roethlisberger faked a handoff to Mendenhall and ran up to the line before pitching the ball to Randle El, who scored on an outside sweep, cutting the Steelers deficit to 3 points at 28–25.</p>
<p>Green Bay took the ball back with just over 7 minutes left, and found themselves facing third down and 10 after two plays, but Rodgers kept the drive going with a 31-yard completion to Jennings over the middle. Starks then ran 14 yards to the Steelers 30. Two plays later, <a href="/wiki/James_Jones_(wide_receiver)" title="James Jones (wide receiver)">James Jones</a> caught a 21-yard pass at the 8. The Steelers defense kept Green Bay out of the end zone, causing them to settle for <a href="/wiki/Mason_Crosby" title="Mason Crosby">Mason Crosby</a>'s 23-yard field goal that gave Green Bay a 31–25 lead with 2:07 left in regulation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pbp_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-pbp-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pittsburgh got the ball back on their own 13-yard line following a penalty on the kickoff. On their first play, Roethlisberger completed a 15-yard pass to Miller. But after a 5-yard reception by Ward, his next three passes were incomplete, turning the ball over and allowing the Packers to run out the rest of the clock.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pbp_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-pbp-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Box_score">Box score</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_Bowl_XLV&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Box score">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistical_overview">Statistical overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_Bowl_XLV&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Statistical overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Nelson was the top receiver of the game with 9 receptions for 140 yards (both career highs) and a touchdown,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> while also gaining 19 more yards on a kick return, all despite 3 dropped passes. Jennings added 64 yards and 2 touchdowns. Roethlisberger completed 25 of 40 passes for 263 yards and two touchdowns, with 2 interceptions, and ran for 31 yards. His top target was Wallace, who caught 9 passes for 89 yards and a score. Mendenhall was the top rusher of the game with 64 yards and a touchdown.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>

<div style="padding:0em 0.25em"><small>1 – From 1966 to 1969, the first four Super Bowls were "World Championship" games played between two independent professional football leagues, AFL and NFL, and when the league merged in 1970 the Super Bowl became the NFL Championship Game.<br/>
2 – Dates in the list denote the season, not the calendar year in which the championship game was played. For instance, Super Bowl XLI was played in 2007, but was the championship for the 2006 season.</small></div>
